Differences Identification: 1. Lord Stevens defines collusion as ranging from the wilful failure to keep records, the absence of accountability, the withholding of intelligence and evidence, through to the extreme of agents being involved in murder. 2. Canadian judge Peter Cory's definition includes several dictionary definitions of the word, such as "to co-operate secretly: to have a secret understanding." 3. Nuala (now Baroness) O'Loan adopts the definitions of Lord Stevens and Peter Cory to examine whether there had been collusion in the murder of Raymond McCord jnr. 4. Al Hutchinson applies a less broad definition in his report on the attack, in 1971, on McGurk's Bar. 5. Sir Christopher de Silva's definition considers collusion to involve agreements, arrangements or actions intended to achieve unlawful, improper, fraudulent or underhand objectives, and deliberately turning a blind eye or ignoring improper or unlawful activity. 6. Irish judge Peter Smithwick's definition aligns with Peter Cory's, including both active acts and omissions or failures to act.  Explanation and Rationale: Output (a) provides a comprehensive summary of the different definitions of collusion provided by various individuals in the article. It covers the definitions provided by Lord Stevens, Canadian judge Peter Cory, the Billy Wright inquiry panel, Al Hutchinson, Sir Christopher de Silva, and Irish judge Peter Smithwick. Each definition is presented in a clear and concise manner, allowing the reader to understand the different perspectives on collusion.
